CHAPTER XXVII. (74).
Ow tHe Praise or Women.

1. Inacountry acquired by aking by conquest the
town is the most important place; in towns, houses are
important places ; in houses, the bed room is an important
place ; in it, the cot and the bed are important, and on it
a woman bedecked with jewels forms the essence of the
pleasures of royalty.

& Gems derive beauty from women; women derive
no beauty from gems ; for, women, when without gems, are
lovely and provoke men’s desires, and not so gems when
alone,

8. To kings straggling to conceal their desires when
in public, anxious to conquer their enemies, meditating on a
hundred schemes of administration either half execnted or
not attempted at all, obliged to follow the advice of their
ministers, ever suspecting fear and failure in every attempt
and buried in a sea of cares and anxieties, the embrace of
an excelleut woman is the only bit of pleasure falling to

their lot.

## Page 358

130 BRIBAT SAMEITA. (cu 97.

4. Inno world has Brahma created a gem superior
to women, whose speech, sight, touch, thought, provoke
pleasurable sensations. Such a gem in the shape of a
woman is the fruit of a person’s good deeds, and from such
8 gem a person obtains both sons and pleasure. A woman
therefore resembles the goddess of wealth ina family, and
must be treated with respect, and all her wants must be
satisfied.

5. It appears to me that those are bad men who, out
of a dislike for all things, speak ill of women, and these men
are never found to speak of the virtues of women.

6. Is there any vice with which women are not
charged by men? Speak-the trath. Those that reject
women do so out of a stupid firmness of mind. According
to Manu, women possess moro virtues than men.

7. Soma-deva has blessed women with personal
purity (a); the Gandhervas have given them pure speech ;
Agni-deva has allowed to them the privilege of eating any
kind of food without restrictions. Women are therefore
without faults.

8. The Brahmins, are pure in their feet (b), the cows,
in their buttocks ; the sheep and the horse, in their face,
aud women all over their body.

9. Women are exceedingly pure and are without
faults. These, (¢) if any, leave them with their menses.

craft, which are cursed by women who are not treated with
respect.

1). The Shastras say that a woman is both a man’s

12, In the eye of the Shastras, adultery in man or

demnation, while women respect it. Hence the superiority
women over men.

18. According to the Shastras a man that commits
adultery shall dress himself in the skin of the ass with the

purification.

14%. Though one might indulge in sexual pleasures
for 100 years, the appetite for the same is nob satinted.

women after the death of their husbands boldly preserve
their chastity, continuing in a state of widowhood.

unlike a thief who, suspecting au iunocent person to be a

22. Beginning from unity form several series of
nambers by adding together each figure with the next and
the sum with the next and so on omitting only the last.
The last of the series will represent the number of combi-
nations reqnired.

Notes:—In this stanza, the author lays down a rule
for finding the number of combinations of n things taken ¢
together when nm and rare known. For instance, required
the number of combinations of 7 things taken 4 together.
Write ina line the figures from 1 to 7 and call it the first
series: thus 1, 2,8, 4,5, 6,7. we vee (I+

Form the second series from the Ist as follows:
14+2= 8; $43 =6;64+4=10; 10+5=15; 15+6=21. So
that the 2nd series is 1, 9,6,10, 15,21... 2)

Form the Srd serios from the 2nd as follows: 14+3=4 ;
44+6=10; 10+10=20; 20415=35. So that the 3rd
series is, 1, 4,10, 20, 3 c we (3)
## Page 376

143 BRISAT SAMBITA. fom. 30.

Form the 4th series form the 3rd thus : 14+4=5;
5+10=15 ; 154.20=35 ;s0 that the 4th series, is 1, 5, 15,35...
(4) and so on. ‘The number of combinations, thorefore, of 7
things taken 4 together is the last numbor of the 4th series,
viz., 85.

The above may appear to be a somewhat clumsy pro~
cess, Bhaskarachariar in his Lilavati (Arithmetic) gives the
indentical rule now found in Western works on Algebra.
He says : Form fractions with the figures, say, from 7 to 1
for numerators, and from 1 to 7 for denominators thus :

bhnhohr

The namber of combinations of 7 things taken 2
together is the product of the first two fractions=21. The
number taken ¥ together is the product of the first three
fractions=35. The nuwber taken 4 together is the pro-
duct of the first 4 fractions=35 and so on. This process
is olso mentioned in the Aphorisms of Pingala known as
Chandas Sutra, a very ancient work, .

CHAPTER XXXI. (78).
Ow Sexvat Uxtoy.

1. King Vidurattha was killed by his queen who con-
ceated a weapon in her plaited hair; and the king of Be-
nares was killed by his queen, who disliked bim, with poison
which she carried in her anklets.

2. Thus wives who do not love their husbands havo
killed them. Of what use is it to quote more instances. Hus-
bands shall therefore ascertain in various ways whether
they have secured the affection of their wives.

3, A loving wife chows her love in various ways. She
will, in the presence of her lord, shew, as if by accident,
ber navel, arms, and ornaments and will adjust her
ganhhents ; will allow the hairs of her head to full loose as
if by accident, will raiso her eyebrows, will tremble, and
will oust a side-look at her busband.

4. Sho will spit aloud ; laugh openly ; get first into the
bed ; crack her joints ; yawn ; boy for the gift of trifles ; em-
brace a child and. kiss it ; will fora time look at her friend 5
look at her husband when his look is turned from her ?
scratch her ears ; and will speak in his praise in his absence

5. A loving wife will, besides, spoak affectionately to
her husband, assist him with her money, will give up her
anger at the sight of her lord and will be filled with pleasur-
able sensations ; will meet any calumnious attacks on him
by recounting his virtues.

6. She will show due respect to the friends of her
lord and hate his enemies ; she will foel grateful to him
for his helps ; will feel distressed during his absence.
## Page 383

ca. 31.] BRIHAT SAMHITA 185

7. An unloving wife will contract her eye-brows ;
turn her look away from her lord; will be wanting in
gratitude ; will not moye from her place at the sight of
her husband ; will never feel cheerful; her lips will be
dull and motiontess ; she will be-friond the enemies of her
lord and will be harsh in her speech.

8. She will sbake with fear at thesight or touch of
her lord ; will feel haughty ; will not attempt to pacify her
lord when he leaves her company in anger; she will wipe
off her face after sexual enjoyment ; will go to bed before
her lord and rise after him.

9 &10. Begging women, female devotees, maid ser-
vants, th nurse, girls, the laundress, the flower-woman, the
harlot, a friend, the barbar woman, these generally serve as
messengers or yo-betweens for women and bring disgrace
and ruin on respectable families ; itis therefore necessary
to protect family women from the intrigues of these per-
sons and to maintain the honor, fame, and respectability of
the family.

11. To go out at night, to keep awake on the pre
tence of a religious observance, to excuse herself on the
false plea of illness, to be found for ever in the houses of
other persons, to attend plays and the like, to consult as-
trologers, to frequent mourning houses or festivals aro acts
from which women should be kept back.

12. A modest wife is one who out of shame does not
first oxhibit an inclination to sexual embrace ; who
throughout is nevertheless subject to sexual passion,

18. The virtues of a woman are young aye, beauty,
decoration with ornaments, being agreeable to her lord,
being learned in matters which will make muried life
happy and being of a pluyfal nature. A lady possessing
these virtues is known asafemale gem, A woman not
## Page 384

156 BRIHAT SAMIBITA [on 31,

possessing these virtues is loathed by a man of taste as
a disease,

Notes.—Vyasa says: A woman who is chaste and
innocent, who eats pure meals, who is of sweet speco and
who is fondly attached to her husband is known as a Laksh-
mi (goddess of wealth).

Again, » woman who has ugly eyes, who is dirty,
quarrelsome, talkative, is known as a Rakshasi (Fury).

14. Awoman shall not indulge in low language ; nor
shall she woar bad colored clothes ; nor be of a dirty body.

15, A good wife is one who breathes unlike men ; who
extends her arms to her lord to serve as a pillow for his
hoad ; the hair of whose head is of good smell, who is fondly
attached to her husband ; who sleeps after him and rises
before him.

16, A woman of a wicked nature and one of weak
health shall be rejected. A woman whose Sonita (blood)
is black, green, yellow, or of eopper color shall also be re~
jected.

17. A person shall not join in sexual union a woman
who sleeps too much, whose blood discharges aro excessive,
who is of an over bilioas, phlegmatic or windy tempera-
mont, who perspires often, who is of defective or oxtra or-
gans and whose hair is short or grey;

18. Whose onlves are exceedingly fleshy, whose belly is
large, who is noisy and who is possessed of other vices des
cribed in the Chapter on the features of women.

19. That blood is faultless which resembles the blood
of the hare or the juice of red-cotton and which when well
rubbed disappears.

20. Tf the blood flow out without pain and noise, and

stops efter three days, there will be conception at the next
sexual union. ,

21. For the three days fromthe day of appearance

22. After this, the vegetable ingredients prescribed
for Pushya Snana shall be brought and put in water and
the several mantras therein mentioned shall be pronounced

the issue will be a beautiful child of long and happy life.

Notes.—Add to these restrictions the number of mal-

Jataka.

Again, according to the Sastras a person shall cease to
cohabit with a woman after the birth of a son—the object
of marringe being thereby secured.

(@) Vide Stauzas 11 and 12 of Chapter IV of the Bribat Jataka,
## Page 386

188 DRIHAT SAMBITA cn. 31.)

Again, the Smritis refer to a number of days in which
cohabitation is prohibited, such as the new-moon and fall-
moon days, the eleventh lunar day and the like. The Rishis
of old appear to have strictly followed ull these rules. If
the whole world could be equally firm-minded, there would
probably be no occssion for so many curious, elaborate and
sometimes oven frightful solutions of the problem to check
the growth of population. You ellow the evil to grow and
then seek a remedy ; but the Sastras aim at nipping the evil
in the bud. Of course when the demand exceeds supply
and a disturbance of the social equilibrium occurs, nature
restores it by applying her own remedy—by carrying away,
every now and then, thousands by wars, by the plague and
the like epidemics,

On the first appearance of the menses: The foor
asterisms from Krittika are known as inner aster-
iems and the four from Ponarvasu are known as the
outer asterisms. Again the four from Magha are known as
inner asterisms, and the four from Chitra are known as outer
asterisms, and 0 on, till we come to the end of the lunar
Zodiac. For a list of the 28 asterisms vide page 87, Part I.
If the first appearance of the menses occur whew the Moon
passes through o1e of the inuer asterisms, there will be
prosperity, incrense of family and the like, If the first
appearance of the menses occur when the Moon passes
through one of the outer asterisms, there will be misery,
widowhood, death of sons, sorrow and the like.

Again, divide the 27 asterisims (omitting Abhijit) into
seven groups of 3,3,8,3,5, 7and 3 asterisms begiuning from
U. Ashadha. If the first appearance of the menses occnr in
any of these, the effects will respectively be gain of wealth,
gain of sons, servitude, sweet speech, ruin, attachment to
husband and widowhood.

sign is Aries, the woman will becomo unchaste ; when it is

rich and happy; if Cancer, she will cohabit with an out-
caste ; if Leo, she will get a son ; if Virgo, she will become
rich ; if Libra, she will become deform~d ; if Scorpio, she
will become unchaste. If the first half of Sagittari, she will
Decome wicked ; if the second half, sho will be chuste ; if

‘become poor and barren ;and if Pisces, sho will become
beautiful.

Also, if the first appearance of the menses occur on a

a Monday, she will become chaste; if Tuesday, she will
suffer grief ; if Wednesday, sho will get sons; if Thursday,
she will live in plenty ; if Friday, she will prosper well ;
and if on a Saturday, she will meet with early death.

Also, if the first appearance of the monses occur in tho
forenoon, the woman will be happy ; if in the afternoon,
she will suffer miseries ; if at noon, she will be neither
happy nor miserable.

within 12 Ghatikas at night, the woman will be happy. To

CHAPTER XXXII (79).
Ow Core axp Sears.

1. As Cots and Seats are useful to all people at all
times and especially so to Kings, I begin to treat of them
here.

2 The wood of the following trees is suited for the
construction of Cots and Seats: Asana (a) Syandana, (6)
Chandana, Haridra, Suradara (c) Tinduki, Sala (palm),
Kasmari (d) Anjana, Padmaka, Saka, and Simsapa.

8. The trees described below shall be rejected: treo
that have fallen owing to an attack of lightning, flood, winds
or elephant, those containing bee-hives or in which birds
dwell, those that grow in places of worship, in cremation
grounds or in roads, those whose barks have dried up or
which are covered with twining creepers.

4. Trees which are covered with thorns or which grow
at the junction of great rivers or in temples or which when
cut fall on the western or southern side shall also be rejec”
ted.

5. If Cots and Seats be made of such trees, the family
will suffer miseries and there will be diseases, fear, loss
quarrels, and the like.

6. If there be the wood of any trees already out down
available for the purpose it shall first be examined : ifs
child gets on it,a person will get cows and children by its
use

7. If white flowers, a rutting elephant, curdled milk,
colored rice, water pots, gems and the like benefic objects
be observed at the time, there will be prosperity.

CHAPTER XXXIII. (80).
On Diamonps.

1. A good gem brings prosperity to the king anda
bad one brings misery. It is therefore necessary to ex:
amine the properties of gems with the help of persons learn
ed in the science ; for a person’s fortune depends upon thp
gems be possesses.
## Page 393

ca. 33.) ‘BRIHAT SAMBITA 165

2. Elephants, horses and women possensed of excel-
lent virtues are also known as gems ; but diamonds and the
like gems to be treated of in this Chapter are stones and
the like possessed of many excellent qualities.

3. According to some, gems are the bones of Balasura
and according to others they are the bones of the sage Da-
dhichi. In the opinion of some, gemsare various sorts of
stones which naturally exist in the earth.

4, ‘Twenty-two different sorts of gems are mentioned :
‘These are the diamonds, sapphire, emerald, karketana, ruby,
rudbira, vydurya, pulake, vimalike, rajamani, erystal or
quartz, moon-stone.

5. Sougandhike, gomedaka, conch-shell, mahanila, to-
paz, brabma-mani, jyotirasa, opal, pearls and corals.

tare of black and white, somewhat bright and mixed with

8. Rubies of superior quality are bright, glossy, pure,
red, and rendering red objects around, dazzling, heavy,
well-shaped and of good water.

4, Gems that are dim, slightly bright, with lines,
mixed with minerals or with gravel, or broken are not good
ones. These are tho faults of gems,

5. A gom of the color of the bes, the neck of the

6. A king who wears such a gem will never suffer
from the attacks of poison and disease. There will be rain-
fall in his country every day in the year and the king’s
enemies will meet with ruin—all this through the virtues
of the gem.

might be given for this gem.

Crystal gems are white like the stem of the lotus or
the conch-shell.

Rudhiraksha goms are groen in the middle, white all
round, as bright as sapphire, of the shape of the fruit of
the Pilu tree (Carea Arborea). It will make the wearer
woalthy and well-served. For farther particulars regarding
gems, the reader is referred to the works of Buddhabhata. -

CHAPTER XXXIX (86).
Generat Roues.

1. Rishabba has written a treatise on omens embody-
ing the views of the Devas Sukra, Indra, Brihaspati,

Kapishthala and Garada and of the Rishis Bhaguri, Devala
and others.

2. Sridovavardhana, the Mabaraja of Avanti (Oojien )

has written a treatise on omens ombodying the views of
Bharadwaja-

S. ‘There aro also treatises on omens by'the seven Ri-
shis; numerous treatises aro also found on the subject
written in ancient and modern languages. Then there are
the treatises of Garga and others who have written works
on Samhita. There are also treutises written by writers
who have written works on Yatra.

4. Having examined all the above treatises I proceed
to write clearly this brief treatiseon omens for the enlighten,
ment of my pupils.

5. Omens indicate to travellers the good or evil effects
of their karma (deeds) in a former birth.

6. Omensare creatures dwelling in villages and forests,
in waters,\in land, in the sky, moving by day or by night
or by both day and night. ‘Their sex shall be ascertained by
their sound, gait, look and speech.

7. Ivis often difficult to ascertain the sex of the crea-
ture and the Rishis have laid down general rules for the
purpose in the following two stanzas.

8, The inale creatures aro generally+those possessing
largo, high and broad shoulders, large neck, fine breast,
short but deep sound and uniform gait.

23
## Page 406

173 BRIHAT SAMBTPA, [ex. 8%

9. Thefemale creatures are those possessing a small
neck, head and breast ; also small face; legs and strength =
and also, a shrill but soft sound, Other creatures belong to
neither sex.

10. In tho present treatise on omens I’ shall confine
myself to matters: relating to travels. What are domestic
animals and what wild shall be ascertained from a general
knowledge of creatures.

11. The effects of omens occurring in roads affect the
traveller and those of omens occurring in armies affect the
king. Omens ocenrring in towns affect the king or the
village deity; and omens occurring before a gathering of
men affect the leader ; if there be no leader and if the per-
sons be all of equal rank those of superior caste, education
or age will be affected by the omens.

12. Dividing the circle of horizon into eight equal
quarters beginning from the east and going round, corres-
ponding to the eight Yamas (a yamais 3'hours) from suurise
to sunrise, the quarter which corresponds to a particular
yama of the Sua in his daily motion is known as Deopta
(inalefic). ‘The quarter next before it just quitted by the
Sun is known as Angari and the quarter next after Deepta
is known as Dhumini. ‘The other five quarters are known
as Santa (benefic). ‘The first three, viz., the Anguri, the
Deepta and Dhumini quarters relate to bad events past,
present and futuro respectively according as the omen
occurs in such quarters. (a).

13, Omens occurring in the three 5th (opposite) quar
ters from the Deepta quarters relate to good events past,
present and fature. If the omen occur in one of the re-
inaining two quarters, the effects are good or bad according

(a). The threo quarters are sometimes spoken of as Deepta quarters.
## Page 407

<u. 39.] BRIBAT SAMHITA. 179

‘as the place more approaches the Senta or the Deepta quar-
ter.

14, Effects of omens occarring in low places will 4o
felt soon ; those of omens occurring in high places will ba
felt late. The increase or tho decrease will follow the
increasing or the decreasing character of the place occupied
by the omen.

18, If the hour, the lunar-dey, the Nakehatra, tho
-wind and thoeun be malefic, the omon is known as Deiva
Deepta (a) and the effects will be of an increasingly evil
wharacter. If the gait, place, sound and motion of the omen
as well as the memory (of the Astrologer) be bad, the omen
is known as Kria Deepta (b) and the effects will also be
-of an increasingly evil character.

Notes.

(a). That is if, at the time of occurrence of an omer,
the hour be that of a malefic plonet, the lunar day be a
analefic one, the Moon pass through a malefic asterisin, tho
wind blow hard and the Sua occupy @ malefic quarter.

(), That is, if at the time, the gait of the animal or
Dird be bad or directed towards bad places, if the plico
occupied by the omen be bad, if the person’s memory fail,
if the sound of the animal or bird be hoarse and if it
should strike its logs or wings cr scratch its face and do
the like.

16, If the character of the omen be the opposite of
what has been described above, the omen is known as Deiva
Santa or Kria Santa respectively. Creatures subsisting on
leaves and fruits are known as Soumya (benefic); and those
subsisting on flesh and excrement are known as Roudra
(malefic); and creatures subsisting on rice and other graius
are known as Sankirna (mixed).
## Page 408

180 BRIHAT SAMIBITA (cu. 89.

17. Creatures found in storied houses, temples, palaces
of kings, places of marriage and the like, in beautiful spots
and on trees where there may be honey, juice, milk, fruits
or flowers indicate good luck.

18. If day-creatures be seen to occupy the tops of
hills by day, the effects will be strong; if night creatures
be seen to occupy waters by night the effects will be
strong. The offects will be of increasing strength uccord-
ing as the creature is a hermaphrodite, a fomale or a mal

19. Creatures remarkable for speed, gevius, strength,
place occupied, merriment, nobleness of mind or good
sound are strong when in their own places; the same rule
applies to useful animals. If the character of the creatures
be otherwise or if they be injurious and if they do not
occupy their own places, they are weak.

20. The cock, the elephant, the parili, the peacock,
the vanjula, the musk-rat, the duck and the kutapoori are
strong in the east.

21, The jackal, the owl, the haritala pigeon, the
crow, the ruddy goose, the bear, ichoumon, the dove, as

well as moans, cries and disagreeable sounds are strong in
the south.

22. The ram, tho swan, the osprey, the francoline
partridge, the cut, as well as festivities, music and laughter
are strong in thewes t.

28, The crane, tho deer, the rat, the antelope, the
horse, the cuckoo, the blue jay and the hedgehog as well as
the sound of sweet-bells and of the conch-shell are strong
in the north.

24, Wild crentures shall not be treated as domestic if
they aro found in towns, and domestic creatures shall not be
treated as wild if they are found in woods. Similarly, doy-
## Page 409

cx. 39.) BRIBAT SAMHITA 181

creatures shall not be confounded with night creatures and
vice versa,

23. Creatures afflicted with the Dwandwa (copala-
tion %) disease, frighteued animals and those that go about
seeking for fight or prey as well as creatures separated by
a river and rutting animals shall not be treated as omens.

26. Tho fox, the goat, the ass, the deer, the camel,
the antelope and the bare shall not be treated as omens ia
the Sisira season (from middle of January to middle of
March). The crow and the cuckoo shall not be treated as
omens in the Vasanta season (from middle of March to that
of May).

27. Tho pig, the dog, the wolf and the like shall not
be treated as omens in the month of Bhadrapada (middle
of Augast to middle of September) nor shall the Abjada,
the cow and the curlew be treated as omens in the Sarat
season (middle of September to the middle of November ;)
nor the elephant and the Chataka (Cuculus Melanoleucus)
be treated as omens in the month of Sravana (July—
Angust),

28. The tiger, the bear, the monkey, the leopard, the
buffalo, and tho serpent, as well as the young of animals
other than human shall not be treated as omens in the
Homanta season (from middle of November to middle of
January).

29. Tho space betwoen the eastern and the south-
eastern points of the horizon shall be divided into 4 equal
parts by threo points, These points are known respec-
tively as those of Kosadhyaksha, Analajivi and Tapoyukta.

20. The space between the south-eastern and southern
points of the horizon shall be divided similarly by three
points known respectively as those of Silpi, Bhikshu and
Vivastra Stri and the three points between the southern and
## Page 410

182 ‘BRIKAT SAMEITA cH, 39]

the south-western points of the horizon are known as those
of Matanga, Gopa and Dharmasamasraya,

31. The space between the south-western and western
points shall be similarly divided by three points known as
those of Stri, Suti and Taskara; and the three points
‘between the western and the north-western poiuts of the
horizon are known as those of Soundika, Sakuni and
Himsra.

82. The space between the north-western and north-
ern points of the horizon shall be similarly divided by
three points known as those of Vishaghataka, Goswami
and Kuhukagua ; and the three points between the north-
ern and north-eastern points of tho horizon are known as
those of Dhanavan, Eekshanake and Malakara.

83. The space between the north-eastern snd eastern
points of the horizon shall be divided equally by three
points known as those of Vyshuava, Charaka and Vajirak-
shake, These twenty-four points together with the eight
points of the compass give us thirty-two quarters in all.

84. The eight points of the compass beginning from
the east and going round are known as those of the king
(E), the first prince (S.H)., the commander of armies (8),
the messenger (S.W.), the heudman (W.), a spy (N.W), a
brabmin (N.), and an elephant driver (N-E.)

Again, the four points of the compass are known as
those of the Kshatriyas (E.), the Vysiyas (S.), the Sudras
(W.) and the Brahmins \N.)

35. The omen in a particular quarter indicates that
the person who observes it whether he be going or seated

will soon meet with the person presiding over such quarter. -

3G. If the sound of the creature be broken, timid,
low, caused by pain, harsh, feeble or dull, it indicates evil.
‘The aatural sound of a joyous animal indicates prosperity.

ex. 39.] DRITAT SAMHTTA 185

87. The jackal, the cuckoo, the Rala, the Chacha, the
ichoumon, the lizard, the sow, the Kokila, and the male of
animals and birds in general indicate good luck when on
the left side.

38, The vulture, the dog, the monkey, the Srikarna,
the muskrat, the peacock, the Sreekantha, the Pippika,
the Raru, thehawk and the females of animals and birds
Jndicate good luck when on the right side.

39. Hissing sound, clapping of hands, auspicious
music, and the sound of the conch-shell indicate good luck
when on the left side, Other auspicious sounds indicate
good luck when on the right sido.

40. The madhyama, shadja and gandhara notes
indicate good luck ; the shadja, madhyama, gandkara and
rishbha notes also indicate good Inck.

Notes—The gandhara note is found only in Deva
oka. The nishade, panchama and dhaivata notes indi-
cate evil.

41. If the sound of the sky-lark, the ram, the peacock,
the mungoose and the king-fisher be heard or if the names

of these creatures be heard mentioned or if the creatures be
seen, there will be gain of wealth; if the blood-sucker be
seen in front of a person there will be misery.

42. If the names of the leech, the snake, the hare,
the hog or the iguana be heurd mentioned prosperity is
indicated ; but the sound and the appearance of these
creatures indicate evil. On the other hand, if the names
of the monkey and the bear be heard mentioned, evil is
indicated, while both the sound and the appearance of the
creatures indicate prosperity.

43. Ifan odd number of animals, birds and the mun-
goose be seen to move from left to right prosperity is indi-
cated and according to Bhrigu the blue jay and the mun-

44. Chikkra, Kutapori and Pirili indicate good luck
if found to move from loft to right by day, and the hog, the
iguana and the snake indicate good luck if found to pass
on the right side.

45. ‘The horse and articles of white color indicate good
luck when in the east; corpse and flesh indicate good luck
when in the south; Virgins and curdled milk indicate good
luck when in the west; and the cow, the Sadhus aud the
Brahmins indicate good lack when seen in the north.

4G. Persons living by the use of the net and by dogs
indicate evil when seen in the east. Those who live by
weapons and by acts of torture indicate evil when seen in
the south. Liquor and hermaphrodites indicate evil when
seen in the west. And wicked men, seats and ploughs in-
dicate evil when seen in the north.

47. On anspicious occasions and on occasions of the
meeting of persons, of battle, of return journey and of search
after articles lost, the omens that pass in the reverse order
to that mentioned for Yatra (journey) generally indicate
good luck. We shall however state the exceptions, and note-
worthy points.

48. On the several occasions mentioned above, omens
connected with the deer, the Rura and the monkey appear-
ing dy day shall be treated as in Yatra and omens connect-
ed with the blue jay, the Vanjula and the dog appearing at
the beginning of day shall also be similarly treated.

49. Omens conneoted with the Naptrika, the owl and
the icheamon appearing at the end of night shall be treated
in the same way as in Yatra. In matters connected with
women, omens described for men apply in the reverse order-

50. Onoceasions of visits to the king, of return-journey
and of entry into mountains, woods and rivers, the omens
mentioned for Yatra apply.

51. Omens on the left side stated to be auspicious for
‘Yatra are auspicious for other occasions if they are found in
front ; and omens on the right side stated to be auspicious
for Yatra are auspicious for other occasions if they are
found behind.

Two birds flying one on each side of a traveller form
an omen known as parigha. It is Kriyadeepta in nature and
points to the death of the person starting on a journey.

52. If these omens be of gentle sound and of agreeable
motion they indicate the gain of wealth and are technically
known as Sakanadwara.

53. According to some the term Sakunadwara is
applied to omens that remain on the right and left sides, that
aro of the same genus and whose sound and motion are
agreeable.

54, If an omen be favorable and another be unfavora.
ble bad luck is indicated to the traveller. He shall bo
guided by the more powerful omen of the two.

55. If a person starting on a journey should first note
an omen stated to be auspicious for return journey and then
note one stated to be auspicious for onward journey success
of object is indicated. Similarly, if & person starting on a
return journey should first note an omen stated to be aus-
pioious for onward journey and then note one stated to be
auspicious for return journey, good luck is indicated

56. If an omen shonld first be found to be auspicioue
and ifthe samo should then stop the journey, the person
who proceeds nevertheless will either suffex death by his
enemy or will engage in fight or suffer from disease,

78. An omen occurring on the top of a tree indicates
the urrival of an elephaut; if it occur in the middle of a
tree, the arrival of a horse is indicated, and if in the foot of
a tree the arrival of a chariot is indicated ; if the omen
occur ina long object, the arrival of human bearers is in-
dicated ; if in one of the productions of water, the arrival of
a boat is indicated, and if the omen occur on a headless ob-
ject, the arrival of a palanquin is indicated.

74. An omen occurring in waggons, in high places,
and in shadows, indicate the gain of an umbrella. Omens
occurring in the east and S. east, in the south and S, west,
in the west and north-west and in the north and north-east
take effect after a day, three days, five days, and seven days
respectively.

73. The lords of the eight quarters beginning from
the east are respectively Indra, Agni (fire), Yama (god of
death), Niruti, Varuna (god of rain), Vayu (the wind),
Soma (the Moon) ard Eesana (Siva). ‘I'he four prime quar-
ters (E,S, W, N.) are masculine and the four sub-quarters
(8, E. 8. W, N.B) are feminine.

76. Omens occurring in the eight quarters beginning
from the east refer to wood in general, the palm, split
bamboo, cloth, productions of water, arrows, leather, and
shawls, and to lotters of advice regarding them. Omous

77. Effects of omens appearing in the eight quarters
beginning from the east will occur respectively in place of
physical exercise, fire, indistiuet sound, quarrel, water,
fetters, mantras and cows. The four prime quarters—E. 8.
W. & N.—are respectively red, yellow, black and white, and
the color of a sub-quarter is a mixture of the colors of the
two adjacont prime quarters.

78. Omens appearing in the eight quarters beginning
from the east, take effect respectively in caves, water, hill,
places of sacrifice and the abodes of shepherds; these are
also places of mecting, fear, Joss and the like referred to in
connection with several quarters.

79. When the question refers to women, omens ap-
pearing in the several quarters beginning from the East
point to women who aro big, young, of defective organs,
dirty, dressed in black cloth, mean,’ tall, aud widowed res-
pectively.

80. ‘The four prime quirters beginning from the East
refer to silver, gold, sick patients and to women and also to
sheep, carriage, sacrificial rite and cow-shed. The eight
quarters begining from the east refer to the banyan tree,
the red’tree, the Rodhra, the bamboo, the mango, the Kha-
dira, the Bilva and the Arjuna trees respectively.

CHAPTER XLI, (88).

On Ominous Catzs.

1. The Kokila or the Indian Cuckoo, the hog, the
Sasaghna,theVanjala,the peacock, the Sreekarna,'the Brah-
mani duck, the blue-jay, the Andirake, the wag-tail, the
parrot, the crow, the dove, tho sky-lark, the wild-cock, the
the osprey, the Haritala pigeon the valture, the monkey,
the Phents, the cock, the Poornakoota and the sparrow are
day birds and animals.

2. The Jackel, the Pingala, the Chippika, the flying
fox, the owl and the here are night birds and animals. If
the day birds be found to move at night or if the night
birds bo found to move by day, either the country will
suffer or the king will meet with ruin.

8. Horses, men, serpents, camels, leopards, lions,
bears, iguanas, wolves, the mangoose, the deer, the dog, the
gost, the cow, the tiger, the swan, the spotted antelope,

cx. 41.] BRIBAT SAMBITA 197

the steg, the jackal, the hedge-hog, the cuckoo, the cat, the
Indian crano and the pigeon are both day and night animals.

4. The Bhasha, the Kootapura, the Karabaka and the
Karayike are birds of the species known as Poornakoota.
The Pingalike, the Pechika and the Hakka are owls of the
species known as Ulukachoti.

5. The Kapotaki and the Syamaare doves of the
same class. The Vanjalake and the Khadirachanoha aro
fowls of the same class. The Chachhundari and the Nripa-
suta are rats of the samo class. The Baleya and the
Gardhabhe are asses of the same class.

6. Srotobheri, Tatakabheri and Ekaputraka are birds
of the same class. The Kalahakarika, and the Rala are also
birds of the same class. The Rala is a bird two inches bigh
and sounds like a Bhringara (a golden pitcher?) at night.

7. ‘The Durbalake and the Bhandika are birds of one
species. If these birds be found to pass on the right side,
they indicate good luck tothe people of the Eastern
countries, Chikkera is a species of animal and Krakavaku
and Kukata are fowls of the same species:

8. Girtakukuta is also known as Kulalakukuta and
Kudyamatsya (the wall-fish) and Grahagodhika are differont
names for the house lizard.

9% Divyaand Dhanvana are animals of the same
species ; Kroda and Sukara are different names for the hog 5
Go and Usra are different names for the cow and Swa and
Sarameya are dogs of the same species.

10. Thus birds and animals bear different names in
different countries. The animals shall first bo identified
from their names and their cries shall then be interpreted
as stated below.

CHAPTER XLIV. (91)
Vi.
On Omens Connected With Wild Animals.

1, If wild animals be found to stay, wander or to
come and go within the limits of towns, present, past and
fature fears aro indicated respectively ; and if they are
found to wander on all sides of the town, such town will
meet with ruin.

2. If, when wild animals enter the limits of towns,
their cry is responded to by the ory of country animals,
villages and towns will suffer miseries; if their ory is
## Page 437

ou. 45.) BRIBAT SAMHITA 209

responded to by the cry of other wild animals, towns and
villages will be beseiged; but if euch cry is responded to
by both wild and country animals, women will be put into
prison by the enemy.

3. If wild animals be found at the gates of towns,
such towns will be beseiged by the enemy ; if they be found ©
to enter the towns, such town will meet with rain ; if they
be fonnd to give birth to their young, the people will suffer
miseries; if the animals be found to die within towns,
there will be fears of various kinds, but if they enter the
houses there will be imprisonment.

CHAPTER XLY (92.)
VII.

On Omens Connected With The Cow.

1. If the cow appear weak and dejected the king will
suffer miseries; if it walk striking the ground with its
heels there will be diseases. If the eyes be found full of
tears or if it be found to fear its own master or to ery at.
tho sight of thieves, there will be death.

2. Ifcows be found to cry when unmolested there
will be ruin; if they cry at night there will be fear; but i€
the ox be found to cry at night there will be good luck. If
cows be found to be tormented by flies or dogs, there will
be immediate rain.

8. If cows while coming home with the ory of bambha
bo found to be in pursuit of bullocks there will. be an
increase of cows in the cow-shed.~ If cows be found wet or
with their hairs on end, or happy there will be an increase
of wealth. ‘The same remarks apply to butfaloes.

CHAPTER XLVI (98).
VIII.
Ow Ougns conNzcrep wita THE HoRsy.

1. If either the part just behind the saddle or the side
of a horse be accidently burnt, evil is indicated. If other-
wise there will be good luck. If all the parts of the body
‘be burnt, there will be misery. If the part be seen to burn
or to smoke, the effects will be felt in 2 years.

2. Ifthe organ of generation catch fire, the master’s
harem will suffer miseries. If tho belly catch fiire, the
treasury will suffer ; if the buttocks or the tail oatch fire,
there will be defeat by the enemy. Ifthe face and the head.
outch fire, there will be success.

8. If the mane, the saddle—back and the shoulders
catch fire, there will be success. If the legs catch fire,
there will be imprisonment. If the forehead, breast, eyes
or legs catch fire and smoke, there will be defeat ; but if
they burn only there will be success.

4. Ifthe nasal pit, the part above it, the head, the
part just below the eyes and the eyes catch fire and burn
at night, there will be success. If horses which are green,
red, black, of different colors or blue catch fire in any part
of their body , there will be the gain of a desired object.

5. If the horse be fuund to refuse to ent or drink or
to fall its legs striking with each other or to perspire for
no apparent cause or to quake, drop blood from the mouth
or to smoke or not to sleep at night and on the contrary if
it be found to sleep by day or be dall or listless with its
eyes closed or to stick its head to the ground, there will be
misery.

6.- If the horse be seen to get upon another horse
when the latter carries a saddle or a man or if the king’s
horse, apparently healthy, be found to meet with a serious
accident, there will be raisery.

CHAPTER XLIX. (96.)
Sopruesenrary TO Osens.
XI.

1. A person learned in the science of omens shall
make predictions taking into account the dik (direction),
place, motion, sound, week day, the Nakshatra, the Muhurta,
the rising sign, the Karana (half a lunar day), the rising
Navamsa and the fixd, movenble and the double nature of
sigas and their strength or weakness.

2. In the case of persons who do not proceed on a

journey, omens are divided intu two sorts—the stable and
the unstable. Omens pointing to the king, the messenger,
the spy and foreign lands as. well as those connected with
troubles and kinsmen are known as unstable.

3. - Omens pointing to death by hanging, abduction of
‘a woman, meals, thieves, fire, rain, festivals, sons, torture,
quarrels and fears are known as stable omens if the sign
occupied by the Moon at the time be a fixed one and they
are known as unstable omens if the sign. occupied by the
Moon at the time of their occurrence be a moveable one.

4. Omens ocourring in hard and firm places, in stone
honses, in temples, in land and in waters ara known as
stable; and omens occurring on weak or moving objects
are known as unstuble—the latter omens point to gain.

5. Owens occurring when the rising sign, the
Nakshatra, the Muburta and the Dik sro watery ones and
those odouiring in water and on new and full Moon
periods and which are at the same tim? deepta (malefic) and
attended with sound point to gain ; also if-the creatures of
water be Santa (benefic) thera will be rain,

creepers when the Karana at the time is Bhadra and when

thieves.

CHAPTER L (97)
On Errzctive Partops

1, Inthe case of the Sun, the effects will occar
after a fortnight ; in the case of the Moon, after a month;
in the case of Mars after the same period as that stated for
the retrograde motion of planets; in the case of Mercury
the effeots will occur before his disappearance aud in the
case of Jupiter, after a year,

2. In the case of Venus, the effects will occur after
6 months ; in the case of Saturn after a year and in the case
of Rahu after 6months. If the matter refers to a Solar eclipse
the effects will ocour after a year and in the case of solar
spots known as T'washta and Keelaka the effects will be
felt that eame day (vide stanzas 6 and 7 of CH ILI Part I).

8. Effects of phenomena connected with the appea-
rance of dark comets will occur after three months ; thoxe of
phenomena connected with the appearance of white comets
will occur after seven days ; effects of halos, rainbows during
## Page 455

ex, 50.) ‘BRIHAT SAMEITA 227

twilight hours and color of the twilight sky and of clouds
will be felt after svevn days.

4. Effects indicated by sbnormal changes of tempera-
ture, by the appearance of fruits and flowers out of season,
by the flaming horizon aid by portents relating to the
motion of unmoving bodies and to tho refusal to move of
moving bodies aud to abnormal births will be felt after 6
months.

5. Effects indicated by portents relating to the com-
pletion of an event without an agent, to earth.quakes, to
severe calamities, to malefle symptoms such as those
connected with homa fire and by portents relating to the
Arying of a wet substance and to the course of rivers will
occur after 6 months.

6. Effects of portents connected with pillars and the
like, with graneries, the temple-images-their speech, weep-
ing quaking and awetting, cattle-fight and fight between the
people of a house during twilight hours and the appearance
of the rainbow at night and lightning will be felt after three
weeks,

7. Effects of portents connected with the increase of
worms, rats, flies and snakes and of those connected with
the sound of birds and animals and with the floating of
lump of earth on water will be felt after three months.

8. Effects indicated by dogs and the like, by the crea-
tures of the village bearing their young in the woods, by
the eutry of wild animals into the village aud the several
abnormal phenomena connected with bee-hives, town gates,
and Indra Dwaja will be felt after a year or a longer period.

9. Effects oonnected with swarms of the jackal and
the vulture will be felt after 10 days. Those of phenomena
connected with mysterious musical sound will be felt that
same day. Those of phenomena connected with disngree-

able sounds will be felt after a fortnight and also effects of

when the Moon passes through the stable asterisms.

of torture, of separatoin or of union shall be commenced
when the Moon passes through the sharp asterisms.

8. ‘The constellations of P, Phalguni, P. Achadha, P.
Bhadrapada, Bharani and Magha are known as (Uggra)
severe asterisms. Acts of disgrace, destruction, deceit,
imprisonment, poison, burning, beating with weapons and
the like shall be done when the Moon passes through the
severe astorisms.

asterisms.

CHAPTER LIT (99).
On Luxar Days ano HAtF Lunar DAys.

1. The lords of the 15 lunar days are respectivey (1)
Brahma, (2) Vidbata, (3) Hari, (4) Yama, (3) Moon, (6)
Subramanya, (7) Indra, (8) Vasu, (9) Sarpa, (10) Dharma,
(11) Siva, (12) Savite, (18) Manmatta (14) Kali and (15)
Viswadeva.

2, The New-Moon day is sacred to the Pitris, A
person shall commence works suited to the Devas presiding
over particular lunar days. The Ist, 6th and 11th lonar
days are known as Nanda; the 2nd, 7th, and 12th lunar
days are known as Bhadra; the Srd, 8th and 18th lunar
days are known as Vijaya; the 4th, 9th, and 14th lunar
days are known as Rikta and the 5th, 10th and 15th lunar
days are known 0s Poorns.

8, Works directed to be done in particular Nakshatras
shall be done on lunar days sacred tothe lords of the Naksha-
atras. The same remarks apply toKaranes and Muhoortes,
## Page 461

cn. 62] BRIHAT SAMHITA 233

4. ‘The lords of the seven karanas Bava, Balava,
Koulava, Taitila, Gara, Vanijn,and Vishti, are Indra,Brahma,
Mitra, Aryama, Bhu, Sree and Yama.

‘Notes:—Karana is half a lunar day. The seven Karanas

mentioned above are known as Adhruva or Movable, and
when eight times repeated occupy the space from the second-
half of the first day in the Moon’s increase to the first-half
of tho 1th day in its wane.

5. The four Dhruva(fixed)Kuranas are Sakuni,Chatush-
pada, Naga and Kimstughna and they begin from the second
half of the !4th day of the waning moon: These are sacred
to Kali, Vrisha, Sarpa and Vayu.

6. In a Bava Karana shall be done deeds o” an
auspicious, a moveable or a fixed character as well as deeds
for the promotion of « person’s health or comfort. Ina
Balava Karana sball be done acts of charity and acts of
help to Brahmins. In a Koulava Karina shall be done
joyfal deeds and those for the acquisition of friends and in
a Taitila Karana shall be done deeds liked by the public at
large and also houses shall be built.

7. Ina Gara Karana lands shall be tilled, seeds sown,
houses built and the like. Ina Vanik Kurana, works of a
fixed nature shall be done as well as dealings with mer-
chants. Ina Vishtior Bhadra Karana, auspicious deeds
shall not be done but acts aimed at the ruin of onemies and
those connected with poison may be done.

8, Ina Sakuni Karana a person shall do acts for the
increase of his bealth and comfort, shall take medicine and
shall learn or repeat theMoola mantras (magical formulae.)
In a ChatushpadaKarana a person shull do deeds convected
with cows, Brahmins, the Pitris and the king. In a Naga
Karana a person shall do works of a fixed nature, cruel
deeds, acts of stealth and wicked deeds. In a Kimstughna

30
## Page 462

284 BRIBAT PAMHITA. [ca. 53.

Karana, a person shall do any work for the increase of his
health and comfort as well as auspicious deeds.

Notes—A Muhurta is 48 minutes. The 12 hours of
day and 12 hours of night are each divided into 15
Muhurtas. Tho 15 day-Muburtas are sacred respectivaly
to (1) Rudra, (2) Sarpa, (3) Mitra, (4) Pitri, (5) Vasu, (6)
Vara, (7) Viswadeva ; (8) Vidhi, (9) Brahma, (10) Indra,
(11) Indragni (12) Daitya, (15) Varuna, (14) Aryama and
(15) Bhaga. The 15 night—Muhurtas are sucred respecti-
vely to (1) Eeswara (2) Ajspada, (3) Ahirbhudhnya, (4)
Pusha, (5) Nasatya (6) Yama, (7) Vanbi, (8) Dhata, (9)
Sasi, (10) Aditya, (11) Guru, (12) Achyuta, (13) Arka, (14)
‘Twashta and (15) Vaya. Ofthe 15 night—Muburtas, the
Ist, 2nd, 6th and 7th shall be rejected for all auspicious
purposes.

CHAPTER LIII (100.)
On Marriage Lagnas and Nakshtras.

1, Marriages shall take place when the Moon passes
through the asterism of Rohini, U. Phalguni, U. Ashadha,
U. Bhadrapada, Revati, Mrigasirsha, Mula, Anuradha,
Magha, Hasta or Swati; when the rising sign is Virgo,
Libra or Gemini; when the benofic planets occupy other
than the 7th, Sth and 12th houses, when the Moon occupies,
the 2nd, 3rd or 11th house; when the malefic planets
occupy,the 3rd, 6th, 8th and 1th houses; when Venus does
not ocoupy the 6th house and when Mars does not occupy
the 8th house ; and,

2. When the rising sign is other than the 2nd, 9th,
or 8th honge from the Lagna in the horoscope of tho bride-
groom or the bride; when at the time the course of the
Sun is benefic ; when the Moon does not occupy the same
sign with the Sun, Mars, Saturn or Venus; or when she is
between two malefic planets ; when the Yoga is neither the

CHAPTER LVII (104).
On The Effects of Planetary motions.

1. The truths of Science have for a long time remained
scattered for want of arrangement. They will become fit
for ready use if arranged and systamatized.

2. The influence exercised by the planets over human
affairs as they move through the signs of the Zodiac is
various. I desire to describe their effects in stanzas written
ina variety of metres and tho learned are requested to
excuse this wish in me. (2).

Notes.

(a). Each stanza of this Chapter is written in a dis-
tinct metre and contains the name of the metre also. On
account of this restriction the ideas expressd in many
stanzas are curious and far fetched.

3. One who has read the works of Mandavya on the
present subject will not like my troatise, and if he likes it
at all, he will like it in just the same way as person will
like his wife whom he knows to be unchaste.

CHAPTER LVITII (105).
On Tue Worsntr Or Tue NaxsnaTra Porussa
Oz Tax Srewas Derry.

1. The asterism of Mula forms the feet of the Naksha-
tra Purusha, The asterisms of Rohini and Aswini form
his shanks ; those of P. Ashadha and U. Ashadha form his
thighs and those of P. Phalgoni and U. Phalguni form
the privity.

2. The asterism of Krittika forms the lip of the
Nakshatrapurusha. Those of P. Bhadrapada and U. Bhadra-
pada form his sides; that of Revati forms his abdomen ; and
that of Anuradha forms his breast.

3. The asterism of Dhanishta forms the back of the
Nakshatrapurusha, The asterism of Visakha forms his
arms ; that of Hasta forms his hands; that of Punarvasu
his fingers and that of Aslesba his finger nails.

4, The asterism of Jyeshta forms the neck of the
Nakshatrapurusha ; that of Sravana forms his ears; thut of
Pushya his face ; that of Swati his teeth ; that of Satabhi-
shak his smiles; that of Magha his nose and that of Mriga-
sirsha bis eyes.

5. The asterism of Chittra forms the forehead of the
Nakehatrapurusha ; that of Bharani forms his head and that
of Ardra his hairs. Thus have been described the features
of the Nakshatrapurusha,

6. A peron shall worship Vishnu and the Naksha-
trapurusha on the 8th lunar day ofthe dark half of the
month of Chaitra when.the Moon paeses through the as-
terism of Moola and shall fast that day-

power.

CHAPTER LIX. (105).
Coxciusion.

1. Platting the hill of my learning in the vast ocean
‘of Jyotisha Sastra and churning it,I have thus brought
‘cout this bright Moon of Science which sheds its light of
kuowledge over the whole world.

2. Oye good men, I have not omitted to mention any-
thing contained in the old Sastras ; you may compare my
work with the Sastras and follow the rules freely.

3, If good critics discover a few merits in an ocean
of demerits, it is their nature to bring the former to the .
notice of the world, while the nature of bad critics is just
the reverse.

4, Exposed to the fire of malicious criticism, the
gold of literary production becomes purified. Every at-
tempt must therefure be made to bring a work to the notice
of severe critics.

5. If, in any of the copies of this work or in the reci-
tation of is by persons who have learned it from their
Freceptors, the learued happen to notice auy portion either
missing or erroneous or omitted, they will, it is hoped, set
ting aside all feelings of malice, correct the error or supply
the omission.
## Page 486

258 BRINAT SAMHIYA- [on. 59.

6. By the blessing of the Sun, the Seges and the
reverened proceptors worshipped by me,I have been able
to write this brief treatise, Salutation to the ancient writers
of Sunhita.

‘END.
